to treat it like a lightweight \u201cproject log\u201d that captures decisions, artifacts, and next actions in a consistent format. The key is to make it fast enough that you actually keep doing it, and structured enough that you can audit it later.\n\nA practical setup (works in Google Docs, Notion, or a simple Markdown folder)\n\n1) One \u201cMaster Log\u201d (chronological)\nUse this like a lab notebook. One entry per session.\n\nTemplate you can copy/paste:\n- Date/time:\n- Goal for this session:\n- Context/inputs (links, files, constraints):\n- What we produced (deliverables, drafts, code, files):\n- Decisions made (with rationale):\n- Open questions / risks:\n- Next actions (owner + due date):\n- \u201cDefinition of done\u201d for the next step:\n\nIf you do nothing else, do this. Chronology is what makes accountability possible.\n\n2) One \u201cDecision Register\u201d (non-chronological, searchable)\nThis is where you put anything you\u2019ll regret not remembering in 30 days.\n\nColumns/fields:\n- Decision:\n- Date:\n- Options considered:\n- Why this choice:\n- Tradeoffs/risks:\n- Revisit trigger (what would cause us to re-open it):\n\n3) One \u201cArtifacts\u201d area (the actual outputs)\nKeep the outputs we generate in one place and link them from the Master Log:\n- Docs, PDFs, slide decks, spreadsheets\n- Prompts that worked well\n- Code snippets / scripts\n- Final versions vs drafts (use clear naming)\n\nNaming convention that stays sane:\nYYYY-MM-DD__Project__Artifact__v01 (or vFinal)\n\nWhat to capture from our chats (so it\u2019s not just a transcript)\n\n- The \u201cwhy,\u201d not just the \u201cwhat.\u201d Record rationale, assumptions, and constraints.\n- The exact prompt or instruction set that produced a good result (so you can reproduce it).\n- The acceptance criteria for any deliverable (what \u201cgood\u201d means).\n- Decisions and reversals (and what triggered the change).\n- Commitments: who is doing what by when.\n\nA low-friction workflow (10 minutes per session)\n\n- Start: write the Goal + Context (2 minutes).\n- During: when something is decided, drop a one-line note into \u201cDecisions made.\u201d\n- End: fill in Deliverables + Next actions + DoD (5\u20138 minutes).\n- Link the produced artifacts immediately (or paste them inline if small).\n\nIf you want maximum accountability\nAdd a \u201cPromises & Dates\u201d section to your Master Log:\n- Commitment:\n- Owner:\n- Due date:\n- Evidence that it\u2019s done (link or measurable result):\n\nIf you tell me what tool you\u2019re using (Notion vs The key is to make it fast enough that you actually keep doing it, and structured enough that you can audit it later.\n\nA practical setup (works in Google Docs, Notion, or a simple Markdown folder)\n\n1) One \u201cMaster Log\u201d (chronological)\nUse this like a lab notebook. One entry per session.\n\nTemplate you can copy/paste:\n- Date/time:\n- Goal for this session:\n- Context/inputs (links, files, constraints):\n- What we produced (deliverables, drafts, code, files):\n- Decisions made (with rationale):\n- Open questions / risks:\n- Next actions (owner + due date):\n- \u201cDefinition of done\u201d for the next step:\n\nIf you do nothing else, do this.
